“I reckon **Kreacher**’s right,” said Harry. “We’re going to have to work out how to open this thing before we can destroy it.”

Sudden awareness hit Harry of what he was holding: what lived behind the golden doors. He felt a violent urge to fling the locket away. Mastering himself, he tried to prise it apart with his fingers and attempted the charm Hermione used to open **Regulus’s** bedroom door. Neither worked. He handed the locket back to Ron and Hermione, who also tried without success.

“Can you feel it, though?” Ron asked in a hushed voice, holding it tight.

“What d’you mean?”

Ron passed the Horcrux to Harry. After a moment, Harry thought he felt something beating inside the locket like a tiny metal heart.

“What are we going to do with it?” Hermione asked.

“Keep it safe till we work out how to destroy it.” Harry replied and, reluctantly, hung the chain around his neck, dropping the locket out of sight beneath his robes beside the pouch **Hagrid** had given him.

## Guard Duty and Unease

“I think we should take turns to keep watch outside the tent,” Harry added. “We’ll need to think about food too. You stay there,” he said sharply as Ron attempted to sit up, turning green.

With the **Sneakoscope** Hermione had given Harry for his birthday set carefully on the table, they shared the lookout role. The Sneakoscope stayed silent all day. Whether due to Hermione’s **protective enchantments** and **Muggle-repelling charms**, or because people rarely ventured this way, their patch of wood remained deserted apart from birds and squirrels.

At ten o’clock, Harry swapped places with Hermione. He looked out on a deserted scene, noting bats fluttering across the single patch of starry sky visible from their protected clearing.

He felt hungry and light-headed. Hermione had not packed food, assuming they would return to **Grimmauld Place** that night. They ate some wild mushrooms that Hermione had collected and stewed in a **Billycan**. Ron pushed his portion away looking queasy; Harry barely ate to avoid hurting Hermione’s feelings.

The silence was broken by rustlings and crackling twigs: Harry believed animals caused them but kept his wand ready. His insides, unsettled by the mushrooms, tingled with unease.

## Fear and Forebodings

Harry thought he would feel elated after stealing the Horcrux, but he did not. Instead, all he felt was worry about what would happen next. It was as though he had been hurtling toward this, but now run out of road.

Unknown **Horcruxes** were still out there, but Harry had no idea where or what all of them were. Meanwhile, he was at a loss on how to destroy the one they had found—lying cold against his chest like it had emerged from icy water.

From time to time, Harry thought he could feel the tiny heartbeat ticking irregularly alongside his own. Nameless forebodings crept upon him relentlessly. Neither can live while the other survives. Ron and Hermione, talking softly behind him, could walk away if they wished; he could not.

The Horcrux against his chest seemed to be ticking away the time he had left. Stupid idea, he told himself, don’t think that…

His **scar** began to prickle. He feared the thoughts made it happen and tried to focus elsewhere. He thought of **Kreacher**, who had expected them home but had received **Yaxley** instead. Would the elf keep silent or tell the **Death Eaters** all he knew?

Harry wanted to believe Kreacher had changed and would be loyal, but what if Death Eaters tortured him? Sick images swarmed Harry’s mind. There was nothing he could do: he and Hermione had decided not to summon Kreacher for fear the Ministry or Death Eaters might come through.

Harry’s scar burned. He felt so much they did not know. **Lupin** had been right about magic they had never imagined. Why hadn’t **Dumbledore** told more? Had he thought there would be time—that he would live for years or centuries like **Nicolas Flamel**? If so, he had been wrong. **Snape, the sleeping snake,** had struck at the top of the tower.

And **Dumbledore** had fallen… fallen…

## Confrontation with Gregorovitch

“Give it to me, Gregorovitch.”

Harry’s voice was high, clear, and cold. His wand was held out by a long-fingered white hand. The man before him was suspended upside down midair, with no visible ropes, swinging eerily, limbs wrapped about him, terrified face ruddy from blood rushing.

He had pure-white hair and a thick, bushy beard: a trussed-up Father Christmas.

“I have it not, I have it no more! It was, many years ago, stolen from me!”

“Do not lie to **Lord Voldemort**, Gregorovitch. He knows… He always knows.”

## Dream and Mind Reading

The **hanging man’s pupils** were wide, dilated with **fear**, swelling until their blackness swallowed **Harry** whole.

Harry hurried along a dark corridor following **Gregorovitch**, who held a lantern aloft. Gregorovitch burst into a room, lighting up a workshop filled with **wood shavings** and **gold**. On the window ledge sat a young man with **golden hair**, who shot a **Stunning Spell** at Gregorovitch and escaped through the window with laughter.

Gregorovitch’s face was stricken with terror.

“Who was the thief, Gregorovitch?” asked a high cold voice.

“I do not know, I never knew, a young man—no—please—PLEASE!”

A scream echoed, followed by a burst of **green light**.

---

## Awakening and Discussion

“**Harry!**”  
Harry woke, panting and with a throbbing forehead. He had passed out beside the tent.

“It was a **dream**,” Harry said quickly, trying to look innocent. Hermione noticed his scar.

“I know it was your scar! You were looking into Vol—”

“Don’t say his name!” Ron angrily interrupted.

“Fine,” Hermione said, “You-Know-Who’s mind.”

Harry explained the dream:

- “He’s found Gregorovitch and killed him.”
- “Before killing him, he read Gregorovitch’s mind.”
- “I saw a young man steal something from Gregorovitch.”

Hermione wanted Harry to rest, offering to take over the watch. Harry reluctantly agreed.

---

## The Thief and the Horcrux Question

In the tent, Harry and Ron discussed the meaning of the dream.

- Voldemort found Gregorovitch, tied him up, and tortured him.
- Gregorovitch could not help make a new wand if bound.
- Voldemort wanted something Gregorovitch claimed was stolen.
- The young thief was merry and wild, reminiscent of **Fred and George**.
- Harry had a faint feeling of familiarity with the thief.

Ron wondered if Voldemort sought something to turn into another **Horcrux**.

Harry was unsure, remembering Hermione’s warning that Voldemort pushed his soul to the limit.

---

## 15. THE GOBLIN’S REVENGE

Early next morning, Harry searched the woods for the oldest and most resilient tree. There, he buried **Mad-Eye Moody’s eye** and marked the spot with a small cross on the bark.

They decided not to stay too long in one place. After removing their **enchantments** and **covering their tracks**, they **Disapparated** to the outskirts of a small market town.

Harry went out under the **Invisibility Cloak** to find food but encountered an **unnatural chill**, mist, and dark skies.

---

## The Dementor Encounter

Harry returned frightened, saying, “**Dementors**.” He could not produce a **Patronus**.

- He felt cold and paralyzed.
- A distant screaming filled his ears.
- It took all his willpower to run from the Dementors.

Hermione asked why he could not cast the Patronus, noting he had succeeded the day before.

Harry felt humiliated and feared something had gone wrong inside him.

---

## The Horcrux and Its Effects

Hermione noticed Harry still wearing the **Horcrux**—the **locket**—and insisted he remove it.

Once removed, Harry felt free and light.

Hermione worried Harry might be possessed but Harry denied it, recalling no lost memories.

They agreed to take turns wearing the **Horcrux** to avoid long exposure.

---

## Hunger and Morale

Ron complained about hunger, having only eaten a couple of toadstools since before.

Hermione and Harry tried to calm the argument.

Eventually, they found shelter on a farm and obtained **eggs and bread**, which lifted their spirits.

- Hermione worried if taking food was stealing but left money under the chicken coop.
- Ron insisted on relaxing, his cheeks bulging with food.
- Hunger negatively affected moods and behavior, especially Ron’s.
- Harry, used to hardship, was least affected by hunger.

---

## Summary

This section explores:

- Harry’s **vision and dream** of Gregorovitch’s torture.
- The mysterious **young thief** and the stolen object Voldemort desires.
- The **psychological and physical effects** of wearing a Horcrux.
- The dangers posed by **Dementors** and Harry’s temporary inability to defend himself.
- The crucial importance of **food** and **morale** during their mission.

## Horcrux Search and Challenges

“So where next?” was his constant refrain. He did not seem to have any ideas himself, but expected **Harry** and **Hermione** to come up with plans while he sat and brooded over the low food supplies. Accordingly, Harry and Hermione spent fruitless hours trying to decide where they might find the other **Horcruxes**, and how to destroy the one they already got, their conversations becoming increasingly repetitive as they got no new information.

As **Dumbledore** had told Harry that he believed **Voldemort** had hidden the Horcruxes in places important to him, they kept reciting, in a sort of dreary litany, those locations they knew that Voldemort had lived or visited:  
- The **orphanage** where he had been born and raised  
- **Hogwarts**, where he had been educated  
- **Borgin and Burkes**, where he had worked after completing school  
- **Albania**, where he had spent his years of exile  

These formed the basis of their speculations.

### Discussion of Potential Locations

“Yeah, let’s go to **Albania**. Shouldn’t take more than an afternoon to search an entire country,” said **Ron** sarcastically.

“There can’t be anything there. He’d already made five of his Horcruxes before he went into exile, and Dumbledore was certain the snake is the sixth,” said Hermione. “We know the snake’s not in Albania, it’s usually with Vol—”

“Didn’t I ask you to stop say that?”

“Fine! The snake is usually with **You-Know-Who**—happy?”

“Not particularly.”

“I can’t see him hiding anything at **Borgin and Burkes**,” said Harry, who had made this point many times before, but said it again simply to break the nasty silence. “Borgin and Burke were experts at Dark objects, they would’ve recognized a Horcrux straightaway.”

Ron yawned pointedly. Repressing a strong urge to throw something at him, Harry plowed on, “I still reckon he might have hidden something at **Hogwarts**.”

Hermione sighed.

“But Dumbledore would have found it, Harry!”

Harry repeated the argument he kept bringing out in favor of this theory.

“Dumbledore said in front of me that he never assumed he knew all of Hogwarts secrets. I’m telling you, if there was one place Vol—”

“Oi!”

“YOU-KNOW-WHO, then!” Harry shouted, goaded past endurance. “If there was one place that was really important to You-Know-Who, it was **Hogwarts**!”

“Oh, come on,” scoffed Ron. “His school?”

“Yeah, his school! It was his first real home, the place that meant he was special: it meant everything to him, and even after he left—”

“This is You-Know-Who we’re talking about, right? Not you?” inquired Ron. He was tugging at the chain of the Horcrux around his neck; Harry was visited by a desire to seize it and throttle him.

### The Founder’s Objects Theory

“You told us that You-Know-Who asked Dumbledore to give him a job after he left,” said Hermione.

“That’s right,” said Harry.

“And Dumbledore thought he only wanted to come back to try and find something, probably another founder’s object, to make into another Horcrux?”

“Yeah,” said Harry.

“But he didn’t get the job, did he?” said Hermione. “So he never got the chance to find a founder’s object there and hide it in the school!”

“Okay, then,” said Harry, defeated. “Forget Hogwarts.”

## Searching for the Orphanage and Continued Journey

Without any other leads, they traveled into **London** and, hidden beneath the **Invisibility Cloak**, searched for the orphanage in which **Voldemort** had been

## Dialogue in the Hideout

“**Six weeks… Seven… I forget**,” said the tired man. “Met up with **Griphook** in the first couple of days and joined forces with **Gornuk** not long after. Nice to have a bit of company.” The sound of knives scraping plates and tin mugs being replaced filled a brief pause. “What made you leave, **Ted**?” continued the man.

“Knew they were coming for me,” replied mellow-voiced **Ted**, who Harry suddenly recognized as **Tonks’s father**. “Heard **Death Eaters** were in the area last week and decided I’d better run for it. Refused to register as a **Muggle-born** on principle, so I knew it was a matter of time. My wife should be okay, she’s **pure-blood**. Then I met **Dean** here, what, a few days ago, son?”

“Yeah,” said another voice, and Harry, Ron, and Hermione exchanged excited glances, sure they recognized the voice as **Dean Thomas**, their fellow Gryffindor.

### Discussion about Muggle-born Status

“Muggle-born, eh?” asked the first man.

“Not sure,” said Dean. “My dad left my mum when I was a kid. I’ve got no proof he was a wizard, though.”

There was silence, broken only by the sounds of munching; then Ted spoke again.

### Escape and Goblin Allegiances

“I’ve got to say, **Dirk**, I’m surprised to run into you. Pleased, but surprised. Word was you’d been caught.”

“I was,” said Dirk. “I was halfway to **Azkaban** when I made a break for it. Stunned **Dawlish**, and nicked his broom. Easier than you’d think; I don’t reckon he’s quite right at the moment. Might be **Confunded**. If so, I want to shake the hand of the witch or wizard who did it—probably saved my life.”

The fire crackled and the river rushed on.

Ted said, “And where do you two fit in? I had the impression the **goblins** were for You-Know-Who, on the whole.”

“You had a false impression,” said the higher-voiced goblin. “We take no sides. This is a **wizards’ war**.”

“How come you’re in hiding, then?”

“I deemed it imprudent,” said the deeper-voiced goblin. “Having refused what I considered an **impertinent request**, I could see my personal safety was in jeopardy.”

“What did they ask you to do?” asked Ted.

“Duties ill-befitting the dignity of my race,” replied the goblin, his voice rougher and less human. “I am not a **house-elf**.”

“What about you, Griphook?”

“Similar reasons,” said the higher-voiced goblin. “Gringotts is no longer under the sole control of my race. I recognize no **Wizarding master**.”

He said something under his breath in **Gobbledegook**, and **Gornuk** laughed.

“What’s the joke?” asked Dean.

“He said,” replied Dirk, “that there are things wizards don’t recognize, either.”

### Goblins’ Revenge and the Sword

“I don’t get it,” said Dean.

“I had my small revenge before I left,” said **Griphook** in English.

“Good man—goblin, I should say,” amended Ted hurriedly. “Didn’t manage to lock a Death Eater up in one of the old high-security vaults, I suppose?”

“If I had, the sword would not have helped him break out,” replied Griphook. Gornuk laughed and Dirk gave a dry chuckle.

“Dean and I are still missing something here,” said Ted.

“So is **Severus Snape**, though he does not know it,” said Griphook, and the goblins roared with malicious laughter.

Inside the tent, Harry’s breathing was shallow with excitement. He and Hermione stared at each other, listening intently.

### The Attempt to Steal Gryffindor’s Sword

“Didn’t you hear about that, Ted? About the kids who tried to steal **Gryffindor’s sword** out of Snape’s office at **Hogwarts**?”

An electric current coursed through Harry, jangling his nerves as he stood rooted.

“Never heard a word,” said Ted. “Not in the **Daily Prophet**, was it?”

“Hardly,” chortled Dirk. “Griphook here told me, he heard about it from **Bill Weasley**, who works for the bank. One of the kids who tried to take the sword was Bill’s younger sister.”

Harry glanced toward Hermione and Ron, both clutching the **Extendable Ears** tightly.

“She and a couple of friends got into Snape’s office and smashed open the glass case where he was keeping the sword. Snape caught them trying to smuggle it down the staircase.

“Ah, God bless ’em,” said Ted. “What did they think, they’d be able to use the sword on You-Know-Who? Or on Snape himself?”

“Well, whatever they thought, Snape decided the sword wasn’t safe where it was,” said Dirk. “A couple of days later, once he’d got the say-so from You-Know-Who, I imagine, he sent it down to London to be kept in **Gringotts** instead.”

The goblins laughed again.

### The Sword’s Truth Revealed

“I’m still not seeing the joke,” said Ted.

“It’s a **fake**,” rasped Griphook.

“The sword of Gryffindor!”

“Oh yes. It is a copy—an excellent one, true—but it was **Wizard-made**. The original was forged centuries ago by goblins and had certain properties only **goblin-made armor** possesses. Wherever the genuine sword of Gryffindor is, it is not in a vault at Gringotts.”

“I see,” said Ted. “And I take it you didn’t bother telling the Death Eaters this?”

“I saw no reason to trouble them with the information,” said Griphook smugly, and Ted and Dean joined in the laughter with Gornuk and Dirk.

Inside the tent, Harry closed his eyes, willing someone to ask the question he needed answered. After a minute that seemed ten, Dean obliged—he was, Harry remembered with a jolt, an ex-boyfriend of **Ginny’s** too.

### Punishment for Ginny and Friends

“What happened to Ginny and all the others? The ones who tried to steal it?”

“Oh, they were punished, and cruelly,” said Griphook indifferently.

“They’re okay, though?” asked Ted quickly. “The Weasleys don’t need any more of their kids injured, do they?”

“They suffered no serious injury, as far as I am aware,” said Griphook.

“Lucky for them,” said Ted. “With Snape’s track record, I suppose we should just be glad they’re still alive.”

### Debate about Snape and Harry

“You believe that story, then, do you, Ted? You believe Snape killed **Dumbledore**?”

“Course I do,” said Ted. “You’re not going to tell me you think **Potter** had anything to do with it?”

“Hard to know what to believe these days,” muttered Dirk.

“I know Harry Potter,” said Dean. “And I reckon he’s the real thing—**the Chosen One** or whatever you want to call it.”

“Yeah, there’s a lot who want to believe that, son,” said Dirk, “me included. But where is he? Run for it, by the looks of things. You’d think if he knew anything we don’t, or had anything special going for him, he’d be out there fighting, rallying resistance, instead of hiding. And you know, the **Prophet** made a pretty good case against him—”

“The Prophet?” scoffed Ted. “You deserve to be lied to if you’re still reading that much, Dirk. You want facts, try the **Quibbler**.”

There was a sudden explosion of choking and retching, plus thumping sounds. Dirk had swallowed a fish bone.

“The Quibbler? That lunatic rag of **Xeno Lovegood’s**?”

“It’s not so lunatic these days,” said Ted. “You want the truth? Xeno is printing all the stuff the Prophet’s ignoring—no mention of **Crumple-Horned Snorkacks** in the last issue. I don’t know how long they’ll let him get away with it. But Xeno says—front page of every issue—that any wizard against You-Know-Who ought to make helping Harry Potter their number-one priority.”

“Hard to help a boy who’s vanished off the face of the earth,” said Dirk.

“Listen, the fact they haven’t caught him yet’s one hell of an achievement,” said Ted. “I’d take tips from him gladly; it’s what we’re trying to do, stay free, isn’t it?”

“Yeah, you’ve got a point,” said Dirk heavily. “With the whole Ministry and informers looking for him, I’d have expected him to be caught by now. Mind, who’s to say they haven’t caught and killed him without publicizing it?”

“Ah, don’t say that, Dirk,” murmured Ted.

There was a long pause filled with more clattering of knives and forks. They discussed whether to sleep on the back or retreat up the wooded slope. Deciding the trees would give better cover, they extinguished the fire and climbed back up the incline, their voices fading away.

### Harry, Ron, and Hermione’s Discovery

Harry, Ron, and Hermione reeled in the **Extendable Ears**. Harry, who had found remaining silent increasingly difficult, now whispered, “Ginny—the sword—”

“I know!” said Hermione.

She lunged for the tiny beaded bag, sinking her arm in up to the armpit.

“Here… we… are…” she said through gritted teeth, pulling at something deep in the bag. Slowly, the edge of an ornate **picture frame** appeared. Harry hurried to help as they lifted the empty portrait of **Phineas Nigellus** free of Hermione’s bag. She kept her wand pointed at it, ready to cast a spell at any moment.

“If somebody swapped the real sword for the face while it was in Dumbledore’s office,” she panted, propping the painting against the tent side, “Phineas Nigellus would have seen it happen, he hangs right beside the case!”

“Unless he was asleep,” said Harry, holding his breath as Hermione knelt in front of the empty canvas, wand directed at its center. Clearing her throat, she said:

“Er—Phineas? Phineas Nigellus?”

Nothing happened.

“Phineas Nigellus?” she repeated. “Professor Black? Please could we talk to you? Please?”

“‘Please’ always helps,” said a cold, snide voice, and **Phineas Nigellus** slid into his portrait. At once Hermione cried:

“Obscura!”

A black blindfold appeared over Phineas Nigellus’s clever, dark

## Conversation with Professor Phineas Nigellus Black

He felt **relieved**; he had been imagining horrors, the **Cruciatus Curse** at the very least.

“What we really wanted to know, **Professor Black**, is whether anyone else has, um, taken out the sword at all? Maybe it’s been taken away for cleaning—or something!”

Phineas Nigellus paused again in his struggles to free his eyes and sniggered.

“Muggle-borns,” he said, “**Goblin-made armor** does not require cleaning, simple girl. **Goblin’s silver** repels mundane dirt, imbibing only that which strengthens it.”

“Don’t call **Hermione** simple,” said **Harry**.

“I grow weary of contradiction,” said Phineas Nigellus. “perhaps it is time for me to return to the headmaster’s office?”

Still blindfolded, he began groping the side of his frame, trying to feel his way out of his picture and back into the one at **Hogwarts**. Harry had a sudden inspiration.

“**Dumbledore**! Can’t you bring us Dumbledore?”

“I beg your pardon?” asked Phineas Nigellus.

“Professor Dumbledore’s portrait—couldn’t you bring him along, here, into yours?”

Phineas Nigellus turned his face in the direction of Harry’s voice.

“Evidently it is not only Muggle-borns who are ignorant, Potter. The **portraits of Hogwarts** may commune with each other, but they cannot travel outside of the castle except to visit a painting of themselves elsewhere. **Dumbledore cannot come here** with me, and after the treatment I have received at your hands, I can assure you that I will not be making a return visit!”

Slightly crestfallen, Harry watched Phineas redouble his attempts to leave his frame.

“Professor Black,” said Hermione, “couldn’t you just tell us, please, when was the last time the **sword** was taken out of its case? Before Ginny took it out, I mean?”

Phineas snorted impatiently.

“I believe that the last time I saw the **sword of Gryffindor** leave its case was when **Professor Dumbledore** used it to break open a ring.”

Hermione whipped around to look at Harry. Neither of them dared say more in front of Phineas Nigellus, who had at least managed to locate the exit.

“Well, good night to you,” he said a little waspishly, and he began to move out of sight again. Only the edge of his hat brim remained in view when Harry gave a sudden shout.

“Wait! Have you told Snape you saw this?”

Phineas Nigellus stuck his blindfolded head back into the picture.

“Professor **Snape** has more important things on his mind that the many eccentricities of **Albus Dumbledore**. Good-bye, Potter!”

And with that, he vanished completely, leaving behind him nothing but his murky backdrop.

---

## Discovery about the Sword of Gryffindor

“Harry!” Hermione cried.

“I know!” Harry shouted. Unable to contain himself, he punched the air; it was more than he had dared to hope for. He strode up and down the tent, feeling that he could have run a mile; he did not even feel hungry anymore. Hermione was squashing Phineas Nigellus’s back into the beaded bag; when she had fastened the clasp she threw the bag aside and raised a shining face to Harry.

- “The **sword** can **destroy Horcruxes**! Goblin-made blades imbibe only that which strengthens them—Harry, that sword’s impregnated with **basilisk venom**!”

- “And **Dumbledore** didn’t give it to me because he still needed it, he wanted to use it on the **locket**—”

- “—and he must have realized they wouldn’t let you have it if he put it in his will

## Emotional Turmoil and Departure

**Harry** repeatedly told himself, "**He’s gone**," trying to numb the shock as he washed and dressed. The harsh truth was that **Ron** was gone and would not return, especially due to the protective enchantments preventing him from finding them again.

**Harry** and **Hermione** ate breakfast in silence. Hermione’s eyes were **puffy and red** from lack of sleep. She **dawdled** while packing, hoping to linger, looking for Ron in the rain-swept woods. Every hope gave way to anger when no red-haired figure appeared, filling Harry with fury and regret over Ron’s parting words: *“We thought you knew what you were doing!”*

The **muddy river** beside them was rising, threatening to flood their bank. After repacking their belongings multiple times, Hermione finally gave in. They **grasped hands and Disapparated** to a **windswept heather-covered hillside**.

## Aftermath of Ron’s Departure

Upon arrival, Hermione dropped Harry’s hand and walked away, sinking onto a large rock and sobbing. Harry felt frozen by the memory of Ron’s contempt. He circled her as she cast a **protection spell**.

They remained silent about Ron for days. Harry vowed never to mention his name, though Hermione’s nighttime crying betrayed her feelings. Harry used the **Marauder’s map** by wandlight, hoping to see Ron’s dot at Hogwarts but found none. Instead, he stared at **Ginny’s name** in the dormitory, hoping she was safe.

## Search for Gryffindor’s Sword

During the day, they speculated frantically about the sword’s location. The ideas became *desperate* and *far-fetched*, with no memory of Dumbledore hinting at any hiding place. Harry’s frustration grew as he realized neither **Ron** nor **Dumbledore** had left a concrete plan. 

Harry faced the painful truth that they had **one Horcrux** but no means to destroy it, and the others remained unreachable. Hopelessness crept in, and he feared Hermione might soon leave him too.

## Companionship of Phineas Nigellus

In near silence, Hermione brought out the portrait of **Phineas Nigellus**, hoping to fill the void left by Ron. Despite previous refusals, Phineas appeared blindfolded every few days, sharing **news from Hogwarts**, though he biasedly supported **Snape** and left when criticized.

Phineas revealed:
- Snape faced a low-level student mutiny
- **Ginny** was banned from Hogsmeade
- Snape reinstated **Umbridge’s decree** forbidding gatherings and unofficial societies

Harry deduced that **Dumbledore’s Army** was active again with **Ginny**, **Neville**, and **Luna** leading.

## Thoughts of Hogwarts and Danger

Harry longed to see Ginny but also missed **Hogwarts** deeply. For a fleeting moment, he fantasized about returning, enjoying safety and care. But he remembered he was **Undesirable Number One** with a **ten-thousand Galleon bounty** on his head, making Hogwarts as dangerous as the Ministry.

Phineas’s probing questions about Harry and Hermione’s whereabouts often ended with Hermione shoving him back into the bag until he agreed to reappear.

## Harsh Weather and Movement

The weather grew colder as they:
- Crossed a **mountainside** with sleet pounding their tent
- Traversed a **flat marsh** flooded with chill water
- Stayed on a **tiny Scottish island**, half-buried in snow at night

Unable to stay in one place, they traveled throughout the country.

## A New Idea and Revelation

One evening, after an unusually good meal—thanks to Hermione’s stealthy supermarket visit under the **Invisibility Cloak**—Harry decided to suggest a new plan. They took a break from wearing the **Horcrux**, which hung beside Harry’s bunk.

Hermione was absorbed in **The Tales of Beedle the Bard**, studying it carefully with **Spellman’s Syllabary** beside her.

Harry tried to get her attention:  
“Hermione, I’ve been thinking, and—”

She interrupted:  
“Harry, could you help me with something?”

She pointed to a strange **symbol** at the top of a page: a **triangular eye** with a vertical line through its pupil.

Harry admitted, “I never took Ancient Runes.”

Hermione explained it was not a rune or in the syllabary, suspecting it was **inked in** later. They debated if Harry had seen it before.

Harry recognized it as the symbol worn by **Luna’s dad** and said, "*Then it’s Grindelwald’s mark.*"

Hermione was surprised:  
“Grindelwald’s mark? I’ve never heard he had one.”

Harry explained **Viktor Krum** had mentioned the symbol carved on a wall at **Durmstrang** by Grindelwald.

Hermione wondered why a dark magic symbol would appear in a children’s storybook. Harry noted that **Scrimgeour**, the former Minister, might have mistaken it for just an eye.

## Decision to Visit Godric’s Hollow

Hermione said, “I really think we’ll have to go to Godric’s Hollow.”

Harry asked for confirmation, and she agreed that it seemed the most likely place to find what they sought.

When Harry asked what “there” meant, Hermione explained that they were looking for the **sword**, and that **Godric’s Hollow** was the birthplace of **Godric Gryffindor**.

Harry admitted he hadn’t read much of **A History of Magic**. Hermione chided him gently and retrieved her copy of the textbook by **Bathilda Bagshot**, hoping to find more information about the village and possibly their quest.

## The International Statute of Secrecy and Wizarding Communities

**Upon the signature of the International Statute of Secrecy in 1689**, **wizards** went into hiding permanently. To protect themselves, they formed **small communities within a community**. Several magical families banded together in small villages and hamlets for mutual support.

Notable villages included:  
- **Tinworsh in Cornwall**  
- **Upper Flagley in Yorkshire**  
- **Ottery St. Catchpole on the south coast of England**  

These villages housed **knots of Wizarding families** living alongside tolerant and sometimes **Confunded Muggles**.

The most celebrated half-magical dwelling place is **Godric’s Hollow**, the West Country village where the great wizard **Godric Gryffindor** was born and where **Bowman Wright**, a Wizarding smith, forged the first **Golden Snitch**. The local graveyard holds many names of ancient magical families, contributing to stories of hauntings at the little church beside it for centuries.

---

## Hermione and Harry Discuss Godric’s Hollow

Hermione points out that Harry and his parents aren't mentioned in **Professor Bagshot’s** book because the history covered only goes up to the end of the nineteenth century. She draws attention to the connections:  
- **Godric’s Hollow**  
- **Godric Gryffindor**  
- **Gryffindor’s sword**

She suggests that **Dumbledore** would have expected Harry to make these connections.

Harry admits he had not been considering the sword when he suggested visiting Godric’s Hollow. For him, the interest lies in his parents' graves, the house where he survived Voldemort, and in the person of **Bathilda Bagshot**.

Harry recalls **Muriel**, Ginny’s great-aunt, who at a wedding mentioned that **Bathilda Bagshot still lived in Godric’s Hollow**.

Hermione is shocked by this and considers the possibility that Bathilda might have **Gryffindor’s sword**. Harry reflects that Bathilda is very old and possibly senile but wonders if Dumbledore could have entrusted her with the sword.

They decide to plan carefully.

---

## Planning the Journey to Godric’s Hollow

Hermione stresses the need to practice:  
- **Disapparating** together under the **Invisibility Cloak**  
- Using **Disillusionment Charms**  
- Possibly using **Polyjuice Potion** for better disguises, requiring the collection of hair samples from innocent Muggles

Harry feels excited, realizing they are about to visit the place where he lost his family and childhood.

After Hermione goes to bed, Harry looks at a **photograph album** of his parents, deepening his emotional connection to the journey.

---

## The Journey and Arrival at Godric’s Hollow

They wait a full week to prepare:  
- Obtaining hair samples while Christmas shopping  
- Practicing Apparating and Disapparating under the Invisibility Cloak

On **Christmas Eve**, they take Polyjuice Potion:  
- Harry becomes a balding, middle-aged Muggle man  
- Hermione becomes his small, mousy wife  

They carry their possessions in Hermione’s beaded bag and cover themselves with the Invisibility Cloak.

When they arrive, they see:  
- **Snow-covered cottages** with Christmas decorations  
- A **small village square** with golden streetlights  
- A **war memorial**, shops, a post office, a pub, and a little church with glowing stained-glass windows

The village is lively with villagers and Christmas carols from the church. Hermione confirms it is Christmas Eve.

---

## The War Memorial and Graveyard

Passing the war memorial, Harry sees it transform into a **statue depicting three people**:  
- A man with untidy hair and glasses  
- A woman with long hair and a kind face  
- A baby boy in the mother’s arms

Harry is startled to see himself represented as a happy, scar-free baby in stone.

As they approach the church, carols remind Harry of Hogwarts Christmases with:  
- **Peeves**  
- The Great Hall’s Christmas trees  
- Dumbledore’s festive bonnets  
- Ron’s hand-knitted sweaters

They enter the graveyard quietly through a **kissing gate**. Snow lies deep and undisturbed along the paths.

They move carefully, checking tombstones and watching for others.

Hermione spots a gravestone with the name **Abbott**, possibly a relation of her friend Hannah.

---

## The Dumbledore Family Grave

Hermione finds and shows Harry the grave of the **Dumbledore family**, inscribed with:  
- **Kendra Dumbledore**  
- Her daughter **Ariana**  
- Dates of birth and death  

A quotation reads:  
> "Where your treasure is, there will your heart be also."

This confirms that both **Rita Skeeter** and **Muriel** were partially correct: the **Dumbledore family lived and died here**.

## Graveyard Reflection

Seeing the **grave** was worse than hearing about it. **Harry** thought that he and **Dumbledore** both had deep roots in this **graveyard**, and that **Dumbledore** ought to have told him so. Yet, he had never shared the connection. They could have visited the place together; for a moment, Harry imagined coming here with Dumbledore, imagining the bond and how much it would have meant to him. However, to **Dumbledore**, their families lying side by side seemed an unimportant coincidence, irrelevant to the job he wanted Harry to do.

**Hermione** was looking at Harry, and he was glad his face was hidden in shadow. He read the words on the tombstone again: "**Where your treasure is, there will your heart be also.**" He did not understand the meaning, though he was sure **Dumbledore** had chosen them as the eldest member of the family after his mother died.

“Are you sure he never mentioned—?” Hermione began.

“No,” said Harry curtly. Then, “Let’s keep looking,” he turned away, wishing he had not seen the stone, not wanting his excited trepidation tainted with resentment.

## Discovery in the Graveyard

“Here!” cried Hermione moments later from the darkness. “Oh no, sorry! I thought it said Potter.”

She was rubbing at a crumbling, mossy stone, frowning as she gazed down.

“Harry, come back a moment.”

He grudgingly made his way back through the snow toward her.

“What?”

“Look at this!”

The grave was extremely old and weathered; Harry could barely make out the name.

Hermione showed him the symbol beneath it.

“Harry, that’s the mark in the book!”

He peered at the place she indicated: a triangular mark beneath the nearly illegible name.

“Yeah… it could be…”

Hermione lit her wand and pointed it at the name.

“It says Ig—Ignotus, I think…”

“I’m going to keep looking for my parents, all right?” Harry said with an edge, setting off again, leaving her crouched beside the old grave.

## Family Graves and Reflections

Harry recognized surnames from Hogwarts like **Abbott**. Sometimes, multiple generations of Wizarding families were represented, but many had either died out or moved away from **Godric’s Hollow**. Going deeper among the graves, Harry felt apprehensive and anticipatory at every headstone.

The darkness and silence deepened suddenly. Harry worried about **Dementors**, but then realized church carols had ended and churchgoers were leaving. Someone had turned off church lights.

Then Hermione’s voice called out sharply.

“Harry, they’re here… right here.”

He knew by her tone it was his mother and father. A heavy pressure pressed his chest, the same grief he felt after **Dumbledore’s** death.

The headstone was only two rows behind **Kendra** and **Ariana**. Made of white marble like **Dumbledore’s** tomb, it shone in the dark, making it easy to read.

---

### JAMES POTTER  
**BORN 27 MARCH 1960**  
**DIED 31 OCTOBER 1981**

### LILY POTTER  
**BORN 30 JANUARY 1960**  
**DIED 31 OCTOBER 1981**

---

**The last enemy that shall be destroyed is death.**

Harry read the words slowly, worried that he had only one chance to grasp their meaning. Reading aloud:

“‘The last enemy that shall be destroyed is death’...” He panicked. “Isn’t that a Death Eater idea? Why is that there?”

“It doesn’t mean defeating death like the Death Eaters do,” Hermione said gently. “It means… living beyond death. Living after death.”

But Harry thought they were not living. They were gone. The words disguised nothing; their remains were beneath snow and stone, indifferent and unknowing. Tears came instantly, freezing on his face. He let them fall, lips pressed tight, looking down at the thick snow hiding where his parents lay—likely bones or dust—not caring that their living son stood so near, alive because of their sacrifice, almost wishing he were sleeping under the snow with them.

Hermione gripped his hand tightly. He could not look at her but returned the pressure, taking deep, sharp breaths, trying to steady himself and regain control. He wished he had brought something to give them; the graveyard was leafless and frozen.

Hermione raised her wand, moving it in a circle through the air. A wreath of **Christmas roses** blossomed before them. Harry caught it and laid it on his parents’ grave.

He wanted to leave immediately. He put his arm around Hermione’s shoulders, she put hers around his waist, and they silently walked away through the snow, past **Dumbledore’s** mother and sister, back toward the dark church and the out-of-sight kissing gate.

## 17. Bathilda’s Secret

“Harry, stop.”

“What’s wrong?”

They had just reached the grave of the unknown **Abbott**.

“There’s someone there. Someone watching us. I can tell. Over by the bushes.”

They stood still, holding each other, staring at the dense black boundary of the graveyard. Harry could see nothing.

“Are you sure?”

“I saw something move. I could have sworn…”

She freed her wand arm.

“We look like Muggles,” Harry said.

“Muggles who’ve just been laying flowers on your parents’ grave? Harry, I’m sure there’s someone there!”

Harry thought of *A History of Magic*; the graveyard was supposed to be haunted. But then he heard a rustle and saw a little eddy of dislodged snow near the bush Hermione indicated. Ghosts could not move snow.

“It’s a cat,” Harry said after a moment, “or a bird. If it was a Death Eater we’d be dead by now. Let’s get out of here and put the Cloak back on.”

They glanced back repeatedly as they left the graveyard. Harry did not feel as calm as he pretended. He was glad to reach the gate and slippery pavement. They pulled the **Invisibility Cloak** back over themselves. The pub was fuller now, many voices singing carols they heard earlier near the church.

Harry considered taking refuge inside, but Hermione said softly, “Let’s go this way,” pulling him down a dark street leading out of the village, opposite their entry.

They passed more houses with windows sparkling multicolored lights and silhouettes of Christmas trees.

“How are we going to find **Bathilda’s house**?” Hermione asked, shivering, glancing back repeatedly. “Harry? What do you think? Harry?”

She tugged his arm, but Harry was distracted, looking toward a dark mass at the row’s end.

Next moment, he sped up, dragging her along. She slipped a little.

“Harry—”

“Look… Look at it, Hermione…”

“I don’t… oh!”

He saw it—the **Fidelius Charm** must have died with James and Lily. The hedge had grown wild since **Hagrid** had taken Harry from the rubble, waist-high grass scattered. Most of the cottage stood, covered in dark ivy and snow, but the right side of the top floor was blown apart—where the curse backfired.

They stood at the gate, gazing up at the wreck of what was once a cottage like those beside it.

“I wonder why nobody’s ever rebuilt it?” whispered Hermione.

“Maybe you can’t rebuild it?” Harry replied. “Maybe it’s like injuries from **Dark Magic** and you can’t repair the damage.”

He slid his hand from beneath the Cloak, grasping the snowy, rusted gate—not to open it, just to hold a part of the house.

“You’re not going to go inside? It looks unsafe, might—oh, Harry, look!”

His touch seemed to trigger something. A sign rose out of the ground through nettles and weeds, like a bizarre fast-growing flower.

In **golden letters**, the sign read:

> On this spot, on this night of 31 October 1981, Lily and James Potter lost their lives. Their son, Harry, remains the only wizard ever to have survived the Killing Curse. This house, invisible to Muggles, has been left in its ruined state as a monument to the Potters and as a reminder of the violence that tore apart their family.

Around the words, scribbles from other witches and wizards appeared, who had visited the place where the **Boy Who Lived** escaped. Some signed their names in **Everlasting Ink**; others carved initials or left messages.

The most recent, shining brightly over sixteen years of magical graffiti, read:

- Good luck, Harry, wherever you are.
- If you read this, Harry, we’re all behind you!
- Long live Harry Potter.

“They shouldn’t have written on the sign!” Hermione said indignantly.

But Harry smiled.

“It’s brilliant. I’m glad they did. I…”

Suddenly, a heavily muffled figure was hobbling up the lane toward them, silhouetted by bright lights in the distant square. Harry guessed it was a woman, moving slowly, afraid to slip on snow. Her stoop, stoutness, and shuffling gait suggested extreme age.

They watched silently as she drew nearer. Harry waited to see if she would turn into a cottage, but she did not. She stopped a few yards away, standing in the frozen road, facing them.

He did not need Hermione’s pinch. It was almost certain she was not a Muggle; she gazed at a house invisible to her if she were not a witch.

Even assuming she was a witch, it was odd to go out on a cold night just to look at a ruin.

According to magical rules, she should not have been able to see Hermione and Harry at all.

Yet Harry felt she knew they were there—and who they were.

Just as he reached this uneasy conclusion, she raised a gloved hand and beckoned.

Hermione moved closer to him under the Cloak, arm pressed against his.

## “How does she know?”

He shook his head. The woman beckoned again, more vigorously. **Harry** could think of many reasons not to obey the summons, and yet his suspicions about her identity were growing stronger every moment that they stood facing each other in the deserted street.

Was it possible that she had been waiting for them all these long months? That **Dumbledore** had told her to wait, and that Harry would come in the end? Was it not likely that it was she who had moved in the shadows in the graveyard and had followed them to this spot? Even her ability to sense them suggested some **Dumbledore-ish power** that he had never encountered before.

Finally Harry spoke, causing **Hermione** to gasp and jump.

**“Are you Bathilda?”**

The muffled figure nodded and beckoned again.

Beneath the Cloak Harry and Hermione looked at each other. Harry raised his eyebrows; Hermione gave a tiny, nervous nod.

They stepped toward the woman and, at once, she turned and hobbled off back the way they had come. Leading them past several houses, she turned in at a gate. They followed her up the front path through a garden nearly as overgrown as the one they had just left. She fumbled for a moment with a key at the front door, then opened it and stepped back to let them pass.

She smelled bad, or perhaps it was her house; Harry wrinkled his nose as they sidled past her and pulled off the Cloak. Now that he was beside her, he realized how tiny she was; bowed down with age, she came barely level with his chest. She closed the door behind them, her knuckles blue and mottled against the peeling paint, then turned and peered into Harry’s face. Her eyes were thick with cataracts and sunken into folds of transparent skin, and her whole face was dotted with broken veins and liver spots. He wondered whether she could make him out at all; even if she could, it was the balding **Muggle** whose identity he had stolen that she would see.

The odor of old age, of dust, of unwashed clothes and stale food intensified as she unwound a moth-eaten black shawl, revealing a head of scant white hair through which the scalp showed clearly.

**“Bathilda?”** Harry repeated.

She nodded again. Harry became aware of the locket against his skin; the thing inside it that sometimes ticked or beat had woken; he could feel it pulsing through the cold gold. Did it know, could it sense, that the thing that would destroy it was near?

Bathilda shuffled past them, pushing Hermione aside as though she had not seen her, and vanished into what seemed to be a sitting room.

**“Harry, I’m not sure about this,”** breathed Hermione.

**“Look at the size of her, I think we could overpower her if we had to,”** said Harry. **“Listen, I should have told you, I knew she wasn’t all there. Muriel called her ‘gaga.’”**

**“Come!”** called Bathilda from the next room.

Hermione jumped and clutched Harry’s arm.

**“It’s okay,”** said Harry reassuringly, and he led the way into the sitting room.

Bathilda was tottering around the place lighting candles, but it was still very dark, not to mention extremely dirty. Thick dust crunched beneath their feet, and Harry’s nose detected, underneath the dank and mildewed smell, something worse, like meat gone bad. He wondered when was the last time anyone had been inside **Bathilda’s house** to check whether she was coping. She seemed to have forgotten that she could do magic, too, for she lit the candles clumsily by hand, her trailing lace cuff in constant danger of catching fire.

**“Let me do that,”** offered Harry, and he took the matches from her. She stood watching him as he finished lighting the candle stubs that stood on saucers around the room, perched precariously on stacks of books and on side tables crammed with cracked and moldy cups.

The last surface on which Harry spotted a candle was a bow-fronted chest of drawers on which there stood a large number of photographs. When the flame danced into life, its reflection wavered on their dusty glass and silver. He saw a few tiny movements from the pictures. As Bathilda fumbled with logs for the fire, he muttered **“Tergeo”**: The dust vanished from the photographs, and he saw at once that half a dozen were missing from the largest and most ornate frames. He wondered whether Bathilda or somebody else had removed them. Then the sight of a photograph near the back of the collection caught his eye, and he snatched it up.

It was the golden-haired, merry-faced thief, the young man who had perched on **Gregorovitch’s** windowsill, smiling lazily up at Harry out of the silver frame. And it came to Harry instantly where he had seen the boy before: in **The Life and Lies of Albus Dumbledore**, arm in arm with the teenage Dumbledore, and that must be where all the missing photographs were: in **Rita’s book**.

**“Mrs.—Miss—Bagshot?”** he said, and his voice shook slightly. **“Who is this?”**

Bathilda was standing in the middle of the room watching Hermione light the fire for her.

**“Miss Bagshot?”** Harry repeated, and he advanced with the picture in his hands as the flames burst into life in the fireplace. Bathilda looked up at his voice, and the Horcrux beat faster upon his chest.

**“Who is this person?”** Harry asked her, pushing the picture forward.

She peered at it solemnly, then up at Harry.

**“Do you know who this is?”** he repeated in a much slower and louder voice than usual. **“This man? Do you know him? What’s he called?”**

Bathilda merely looked vague. Harry felt an awful frustration. How had **Rita Skeeter** unlocked Bathilda’s memories?

**“Who is this man?”** he repeated loudly.

**“Harry, what are you doing?”** asked Hermione.

**“This picture. Hermione, it’s the thief, the thief who stole from Gregorovitch! Please!”** he said to Bathilda. **“Who is this?”**

But she only stared at him.

**“Why did you ask us to come with you, Mrs.—Miss—Bagshot?”** asked Hermione, raising her own voice. **“Was there something you wanted to tell us?”**

Giving no sign that she had heard Hermione, Bathilda now shuffled a few steps closer to Harry. With a little jerk of her head she looked back into the hall.

**“You want us to leave?”** he asked.

She repeated the gesture, this time pointing firstly at him, then at herself, then at the ceiling.

**“Oh, right… Hermione, I think she wants me to go upstairs with her.”**

**“All right,”** said Hermione, **“let’s go.”**

But when Hermione moved, Bathilda shook her head with surprising vigor, once more pointing first at Harry, then to herself.

**“She wants me to go with her, alone.”**

**“Why?”** asked Hermione, and her voice rang out sharp and clear in the candlelit room, the old lady shook her head a little at the loud noise.

**“Maybe Dumbledore told her to give the sword to me, and only to me?”**

**“Do you really think she knows who you are?”**

**“Yes,”** said Harry, looking down into the milky eyes fixed upon his own. **“I think she does.”**

**“Well, okay then, but be quick, Harry.”**

**“Lead the way,”** Harry told Bathilda.

She seemed to understand, because she shuffled around him toward the door. Harry glanced back at Hermione with a reassuring smile, but he was not sure she had seen it; she stood hugging herself in the midst of the candlelit squalor, looking toward the bookcase. As Harry walked out of the room, unseen by both Hermione and Bathilda, he slipped the silver-framed photograph of the unknown thief inside his jacket.

The stairs were steep and narrow; Harry was half tempted to place his hands on stout Bathilda’s backside to ensure that she did not topple over backward on top of him, which seemed only too likely. Slowly, wheezing a little, she climbed to the upper landing, turned immediately right, and led him into a low-ceilinged bedroom.

It was pitch-black and smelled horrible: Harry had just made out a chamber pot protruding from under the bed before Bathilda closed the door and even that was swallowed by the darkness.

**“Lumos,”** said Harry, and his wand ignited. He gave a start: Bathilda had moved close to him in those few seconds of darkness, and he had not heard her approach.

**“You are Potter?”** she whispered.

**“Yes, I am.”**

She nodded slowly, solemnly. Harry felt the Horcrux beating fast, faster than his own heart; It was an unpleasant, agitating sensation.

**“Have you got anything for me?”** Harry asked, but she seemed distracted by his lit wand-tip.

**“Have you got anything for me?”** he repeated.

Then she closed her eyes and several things happened at once: Harry’s scar prickled painfully; the Horcrux twitched so that the front of his sweater actually moved; the dark, fetid room dissolved momentarily. He felt a leap of joy and spoke in a high, cold voice: **Hold him!**

Harry swayed where he stood: The dark, foul-smelling room seemed to close around him again; he did not know what had just happened.

**“Have you got anything for me?”** he asked for a third time, much louder.

**“Over here,”** she whispered, pointing to the corner. Harry raised his wand and saw the outline of a cluttered dressing table beneath the curtained window.

This time she did not lead him. Harry edged between her and the unmade bed, his wand raised. He did not want to look away from her.

**“What is it?”** he asked as he reached the dressing table, which was heaped high with what looked and smelled like dirty laundry.

**“There,”** she said, pointing at the shapeless mass.

And in the instant that he looked away, his eyes taking the tangled mess for a sword hilt, a ruby, she moved weirdly: He saw it out of the corner of his eye; panic made him turn and horror paralyzed him as he saw the old body collapsing and the great snake pouring from the place where her neck had been.

The snake struck as he raised his wand: The force of the bite to his forearm sent the wand spinning up toward the ceiling; its light swung dizzyingly around the room and was extinguished; Then a powerful blow from the tail to his midriff knocked the breath out of him: He fell backward onto the dressing table, into the mound of filthy clothing—

He rolled sideways, narrowly avoiding the snake’s tail, which thrashed down upon the table where he had been a second earlier. Fragments of the glass surface rained upon him as he hit the floor. From below he heard Hermione call, **“Harry?”**

He could not get enough breath into his lungs to call back: Then a heavy smooth mass smashed him to the floor and he felt it slide over him, powerful, muscular—

**“No!”** he gasped, pinned to the floor.

**“Yes,”** whispered the voice. **“Yesss… hold you… hold you…”**

**“Accio… Accio Wand…”**

But nothing happened and he needed his hands to try to force the snake from him as it coiled itself around his torso, squeezing the air from him, pressing the Horcrux hard into his chest, a circle of ice that throbbed with life, inches from his own frantic heart, and his brain was flooding with cold, white light, all thought obliterated, his own breath drowned, distant footsteps, everything going…

A metal heart was banging outside his chest, and now he was flying, flying with triumph in his heart, without need of broomstick or thestral…

He was abruptly awake in the sour-smelling darkness; **Nagini** had released him. He scrambled up and saw the snake outlined against the landing light: It struck, and Hermione dived aside with a shriek; her deflected curse hit the curtained window, which shattered. Frozen air filled the room as Harry ducked to avoid another shower of broken glass and his foot slipped on a pencil-like something—his wand—

He bent and snatched it up, but now the room was full of the snake, its tail thrashing; Hermione was nowhere to be seen and for a moment Harry thought the worst, but then there was a loud bang and a flash of red light, and the snake flew into the air, smacking Harry hard in the face as it went, coil after heavy coil rising up to the ceiling. Harry raised his wand, but as he did so, his scar seared more painfully, more powerfully than it had done in years.

## Narrative: The Attack at Bathilda’s House

**“He’s coming! Hermione, he’s coming!”**  
The chaos began as the **snake** fell, hissing wildly. Shelves smashed, china shattered, and Harry grabbed **Hermione** as the danger escalated.  

Hermione shrieked in pain as Harry pulled her back. The **snake lunged**, but Harry took a running leap dragging Hermione; she yelled, **“Confringo!”**, sending a spell exploding the mirror and ricocheting around the room. Harry felt heat sear his hand as they leapt through the broken window. 

Harry’s **scar** burst open with pain, and suddenly he was **Voldemort** again, running through the fetid room, clutching at the windowsill, screaming with rage. The scream mingled with a girl’s and echoed across the dark garden under the Christmas bells.  

## Harry’s Torment and Transformation

Harry's pain was overwhelming; his **head hurt terribly**, yet he questioned if he was dead since pain should cease with death. The wet, windy night surrounded him, with two children in pumpkin costumes nearby, and **Muggle** decorations of spiders on windows.   

Harry moved silently, feeling **triumph** rather than anger, knowing his purpose and power. A small boy smiled at him, but the smile faltered when the boy saw Harry’s face beneath the hood.  

Harry fingered his **wand**, but chose not to harm the child.

## The Entrance into the Potter House

Harry moved along a dark street, arriving where the **Fidelius Charm** was broken without others knowing. He saw the family through the window: a tall black-haired man (James Potter), a small boy (Harry), and the mother entering.

The father yawned and threw down his wand as he handed his son to the mother. Harry pushed the gate and silently entered.  

## The Attack on the Potters

James Potter sprinted into the hall without his wand. He shouted for Lily to take Harry and run while he held off the attacker.

Without a wand, James laughed and cast **“Avada Kedavra!”**. The **green light** filled the hallway, and James fell dead like a marionette.  

The attacker climbed upstairs, amused by Lily’s attempts to barricade herself. She had no wand and was trusting, thinking they were safe without weapons.  

He forced open the door, cast aside the barriers, and found Lily with the child. She begged **“Not Harry! Please, take me instead!”**  

The attacker warned her to stand aside but eventually cast **“Avada Kedavra!”** and she fell.  

The child did not cry all this time but began once he saw the attacker was not James.  

Harry raised his wand to kill the child with **“Avada Kedavra!”** but then broke down in terror and pain, crying **“No…”**  

## The Snake and Memory at Bathilda’s House

The snake rustled on the floor among broken china. Harry was torn: he had killed the child but was also the child.  

Now at the broken window of **Bathilda’s house**, immersed in memories of loss, the snake slithered at his feet. He saw something incredible and whispered repeatedly, **“No…”**  

## Harry Awakens: Reality and Recovery

**“Harry, it’s all right, you’re all right!”** Hermione whispered as he woke. He was in a tent, lying on a bunk beneath blankets.  

He could tell dawn was near by the flat light outside. Harry was drenched in sweat and felt exhausted.  

Hermione explained she used a **Hover Charm** to get him into bed as he couldn’t move. He had been ill.  

### Hermione’s Care and the Horcrux

Hermione held a sponge, wiping his face gently. Harry noticed purple shadows under her eyes. She said:  

- Harry hadn’t fully been unconscious, rather shouting and moaning in distress.  
- The **Horcrux** stuck to his chest, leaving a **mark** and needing a **Severing Charm** to remove.  
- The snake had hit him, causing wounds now treated with dittany.  

Harry saw the **scarlet oval** on his chest and puncture marks on his forearm.  

### Consequences of the Horcrux and Guilt

The locket Horcrux was now in Hermione’s bag for safekeeping.  

Harry expressed regret for going to **Godric’s Hollow**. Hermione said she wanted to go too, hoping Dumbledore left the sword there. They both agreed they were mistaken.  

### The Truth about Bathilda and the Snake

Hermione asked what happened upstairs. Harry explained:  

- The snake was hiding inside Bathilda herself, placed there by **You-Know-Who** to wait for Harry.  
- Bathilda was dead for some time.  
- The snake’s speech was **Parseltongue**, which Harry could understand.  
- The snake sent a message to Voldemort to keep Harry trapped.  
- Bathilda then transformed into the snake and attacked Harry.  

The snake’s attack was meant to **capture** not kill him until Voldemort arrived.

## The Broken Wand

Harry decided to stay awake, despite Hermione urging him to rest. She looked exhausted but cared for him.  

Harry asked for his wand, which Hermione hesitated to give.  

The broken **holly and phoenix feather wand** was nearly severed in two, held only by a single feather strand.  

Harry treated it like a living being and asked Hermione to mend it. She reluctantly cast **“Reparo”**.  

The wand resealed but was weak: It sparked feebly with **“Lumos”**, then went out.  

Harry tried **“Expelliarmus”** on Hermione; the wand split again, showing its damage.  

Hermione tearfully explained she had accidentally hit the wand with a **Blasting Curse** rebound while escaping the snake at Bathilda’s.  

Harry accepted it was an accident and resolved:  

_“We’ll—we’ll find a way to repair it.”_

## 18. THE LIFE AND LIES OF ALBUS DUMBLEDORE

“**Harry**, I don’t think we’re going to be able to,” said **Hermione**, the ears trickling down her face. “Remember… remember **Ron**? When he broke his wand, crashing the car? It was never the same again, he had to get a new one.”

**Harry** thought of **Ollivander**, kidnapped and held hostage by **Voldemort**; of **Gregorovitch**, who was dead. How was he supposed to find himself a new wand?

“Well,” he said, in a falsely matter-of-fact voice, “well, I’ll just borrow **yours** for now, then. While I keep watch.”

Her face glazed with tears, **Hermione** handed over her wand, and he left her sitting beside his bed, desiring nothing more than to get away from her.

---

The sun was coming up: The pure, colorless vastness of the sky stretched over him, indifferent to him and his suffering. **Harry** sat down in the tent entrance and took a deep breath of clean air. Simply to be alive to watch the sun rise over the sparkling snowy hillside ought to have been the greatest treasure on earth, yet he could not appreciate it: His senses had been spiked by the calamity of losing his wand. He looked out over a valley blanketed in snow, distant church bells chiming through the glittering silence.

Without realizing it, he was digging his fingers into his arms as if he were trying to resist physical pain. He had spilled his own blood more times than he could count; he had lost all bones in his right arm once; this journey had already given him scars to his chest and forearm to join those on his hand and forehead, but never, until this moment, had he felt himself to be fatally weakened, vulnerable, and naked, as though the best part of his **magical power** had been torn from him. He knew exactly what **Hermione** would say if he expressed any of this: **The wand is only as good as the wizard**. But she was wrong, his case was different. She had not felt the wand spin like the needle of a compass and shoot golden flames at his enemy. He had lost the protection of the **twin cores**, and only now that it was gone did he realize how much he had been counting on it.

He pulled the pieces of the broken wand out of his pocket and, without looking at them, tucked them away in **Hagrid’s pouch** around his neck. The pouch was now too full of broken and useless objects to take any more. **Harry’s** hand brushed the old **Snitch** through the mokeskin and for a moment he had to fight the temptation to pull it out and throw it away. **Impenetrable**, **unhelpful**, **useless**, like everything else **Dumbledore** had left behind—

And his fury at **Dumbledore** broke over him now like lava, scorching him inside, wiping out every other feeling. Out of sheer desperation they had talked themselves into believing that **Godric’s Hollow** held answers, convinced themselves that they were supposed to go back, that it was all part of some secret path laid out for them by **Dumbledore**: but there was no map, no plan. **Dumbledore** had left them to grope in the darkness, to wrestle with unknown and undreamed-of terrors, alone and unaided: Nothing was explained, nothing was given freely, they had no sword, and now, **Harry** had no wand. And he had dropped the photograph of the thief, and it would surely be easy now for **Voldemort** to find out who he was…

**Voldemort** had all the information now…

“Harry?”

**Hermione** looked frightened that he might curse her with her own wand. Her face streaked with tears, she crouched down beside him, two cups of tea trembling in her hands and something bulky under her arm.

“Thanks,” he said, taking one of the cups.

“Do you mind if I talk to you?”

“No,” he said because he did not want to hurt her feelings.

“Harry, you wanted to know who that man in the picture was. Well… I’ve got the book.”

Timidly she pushed it onto his lap, a pristine copy of **The Life and Lies of Albus Dumbledore**.

“Where—how—?”

“It was in **Bathilda’s** sitting room, just lying there… This note was sticking out of the top of it.”

**Hermione** read the few lines of spiky, acid-green writing aloud.

“‘Dear **Batty**, Thanks for your help. Here’s a copy of the book, hope you like it. You said everything, even if you don’t remember it. **Rita**.’ I think it must have arrived while the real **Bathilda** was alive, but perhaps she wasn’t in any fit state to read it?”

“No, she probably wasn’t.”

**Harry** looked down upon **Dumbledore’s** face and experienced a surge of savage pleasure: Now he would know if all the things that **Dumbledore** had never thought it worth telling him, whether **Dumbledore** wanted him to or not.

“You’re still really angry at me, aren’t you?” said **Hermione**; he looked up to see fresh tears leaking out of her eyes, and knew that his anger must have shown in his face.

“No,” he said quietly. “No, **Hermione**, I know it was an accident. You were trying to get us out of there alive, and you were incredible. I’d be dead if you hadn’t been there to help me.”

He tried to return her watery smile, then turned his attention to the book. Its spine was stiff; it had clearly never been opened before. He riffled through the pages, looking for photographs. He came across the one he sought almost at once, the young **Dumbledore** and his handsome companion, roaring with laughter at some long-forgotten joke. **Harry** dropped his eyes to the caption.

**Albus Dumbledore, shortly after his mother’s death, with his friend Gellert Grindelwald.**

**Harry** gaped at the last word for several long moments. **Grindelwald**. His friend **Grindelwald**. He looked sideways at **Hermione**, who was still contemplating the name as though she could not believe her eyes. Slowly she looked up at **Harry**.

“**Grindelwald!**”

Ignoring the remainder of the photographs, **Harry** searched the pages around them for a recurrence of that fatal name. He soon discovered it and read greedily, but became lost: It was necessary to go farther back to make sense of it all, and eventually he found himself at the start of a chapter entitled **“The Greater Good.”** Together, he and **Hermione** started to read:

---

### The Greater Good

Now approaching his eighteenth birthday, **Dumbledore** left **Hogwarts** in a blaze of glory—Head Boy, Prefect, Winner of the **Barnabus Finkley Prize for Exceptional Spell-Casting**, British Youth Representative to the **Wizengamot**, Gold Medal-Winner for Ground-Breaking Contribution to the International Alchemical Conference in Cairo.

**Dumbledore** intended, next, to take a Grand Tour with **Elphias “Dogbreath” Doge**, the dim-witted but devoted sidekick he had picked up at school.

The two young men were staying at the **Leaky Cauldron** in London, preparing to depart for Greece the following morning, when an owl arrived bearing news of **Dumbledore’s mother’s death**. **“Dogbreath” Doge**, who refused to be interviewed for this book, has given the public his own sentimental version of what happened next. He represents **Kendra’s death** as a tragic blow, and **Dumbledore’s decision to give up his expedition** as an act of noble self-sacrifice.

Certainly **Dumbledore** returned to **Godric’s Hollow** at once, supposedly to “care” for his younger brother and sister. But how much care did he actually give them?

“He were a head case, that **Aberforth**,” said **Enid Smeek**, whose family lived on the outskirts of **Godric’s Hollow** at that time. “Ran wild. ’Course, with his mum and dad gone you’d have felt sorry for him, only he kept chucking goat dung at my head. I don’t think **Albus** was fussed about him. I never saw them together, anyway.”

So what was **Albus** doing, if not comforting his wild young brother? The answer, it seems, is ensuring the continued imprisonment of his sister. For though her first jailer had died, there was no change in the pitiful condition of **Ariana Dumbledore**. Her very existence continued to be known only to those few outsiders who, like **“Dogbreath” Doge**, could be counted upon to believe in the story of her “ill health.”

Another such easily satisfied friend of the family was **Bathilda Bagshot**, the celebrated magical historian who has lived in **Godric’s Hollow** for many years. **Kendra**, of course, had rebuffed **Bathilda** when she first attempted to welcome the family to the village. Several years later, however, the author sent an owl to **Albus** at **Hogwarts**, having been favorably impressed by his paper on trans-species transformation in **Transfiguration Today**. This initial contract led to acquaintance with the entire **Dumbledore** family. At the time of **Kendra’s death**, **Bathilda** was the only person in **Godric’s Hollow** who was on speaking terms with **Dumbledore’s mother**.

Unfortunately, the brilliance that **Bathilda** exhibited earlier in her life has now dimmed. “The fire’s lit, but the cauldron’s empty,” as **Ivor Dillonsby** put it to me, or, in **Enid Smeek’s** slightly earthier phrase, “She’s nutty as squirrel poo.” Nevertheless, a combination of tried-and-tested reporting techniques enabled me to extract enough nuggets of hard fact to string together the whole scandalous story.

Like the rest of the **Wizarding world**, **Bathilda** puts **Kendra’s premature death** down to a backfiring charm, a story repeated by **Albus** and **Aberforth** in later years. **Bathilda** also parrots the family line on **Ariana**, calling her “frail” and “delicate.” On one subject, however, **Bathilda** is well worth the effort I put into procuring **Veritaserum**, for she, and she alone, knows the full story of the best-kept secret of **Albus Dumbledore’s life**. Now revealed for the first time, it calls into question everything that his admirers believed of **Dumbledore**: his supposed hatred of the **Dark Arts**, his opposition to the oppression of **Muggles**, even his devotion to his own family.

---

### Gellert Grindelwald

The very same summer that **Dumbledore** went home to **Godric’s Hollow**, now an orphan and head of the family, **Bathilda Bagshot** agreed to accept into her home her great-nephew, **Gellert Grindelwald**.

The name of **Grindelwald** is justly famous: In a list of **Most Dangerous Dark Wizards of All Time**, he would miss out on the top spot only because **You-Know-Who** arrived, a generation later, to steal his crown. As **Grindelwald** never extended his campaign of terror to Britain, however, the details of his rise to power are not widely known here.

Educated at **Durmstrang**, a school famous even then for its unfortunate tolerance of the **Dark Arts**, **Grindelwald** showed himself quite as precociously brilliant as **Dumbledore**. Rather than channel his abilities into the attainment of awards and prizes, however, **Gellert Grindelwald** devoted himself to no other pursuits. At sixteen years old, even **Durmstrang** felt it could no longer turn a blind eye to the twisted experiments of **Gellert Grindelwald**, and he was **expelled**.

Hitherto, all that has been known of **Grindelwald’s** next movements is that he “traveled around for some months.” It can now be revealed that **Grindelwald** chose to visit his great-aunt in **Godric’s Hollow**, and that there, intensely shocking though it will be for many to hear it, he struck up a close friendship with none other than **Albus Dumbledore**.

“He seemed a charming boy to me,” babbles **Bathilda**, “whatever he became later. Naturally I introduced him to poor **Albus**, who was missing the company of lads his own age. The boys took to each other at once.”

They certainly did. **Bathilda** shows me a letter, kept by her that **Albus Dumbledore** sent **Gellert Grindelwald** in the dead of night.

“Yes, even after they’d spent all day in discussion—both such brilliant young boys, they got on like a cauldron on fire—I’d sometimes hear an owl tapping at **Gellert’s** bedroom window, delivering a letter from **Albus**! An idea would have struck him and he had to let **Gellert** know immediately!”

And what ideas they were. Profoundly shocking though **Albus Dumbledore’s** fans will find it, here are the thoughts of their seventeen-year-old hero, as relayed to his new best friend. (A copy of the original letter may be seen on page 463.)

**Gellert—**

## Letter from Albus Dumbledore on Wizard Dominance

Your point about **Wizard dominance being FOR THE MUGGLES’ OWN GOOD**—this, I think, is the crucial point. Yes, we have been given **power** and yes, that power gives us the **right to rule**, but it also gives us **responsibilities over the ruled**. We must stress this point, it will be the **foundation stone** upon which we build.

Where we are opposed, as we surely will be, this must be the basis of all our **counterarguments**. We seize control **FOR THE GREATER GOOD**. And from this it follows that where we meet resistance, we must use **only the force that is necessary and no more**. (This was your mistake at Durmstrang! But I do not complain, because if you had not been expelled, we would never have met.)

- **Albus**

---

## The Statute of Secrecy and its Implications

Astonished and appalled though his many admirers will be, this letter constitutes the **Statute of Secrecy** and establishing **Wizard rule over Muggles**. What a blow for those who have always portrayed **Dumbledore as the Muggle-borns’ greatest champion**! How hollow those speeches promoting **Muggle rights** seem in the light of this damning new evidence!

How despicable does **Albus Dumbledore** appear, busy plotting his rise to power when he should have been mourning his mother and caring for his sister!

---

## The Rupture Between Dumbledore and Grindelwald

No doubt those determined to keep Dumbledore on his crumbling pedestal will claim:

- He did not put his plans into action.
- He must have suffered a **change of heart**.
- He came to his senses.

However, the truth seems altogether more shocking.

Barely two months into their great new friendship, **Dumbledore and Grindelwald parted**, never to see each other again until their legendary duel (see chapter 22). What caused this abrupt rupture?

- Had Dumbledore told Grindelwald he wanted no more part in his plans? Alas, no.

Bathilda recounts:

> “It was poor little **Ariana dying** that did it. It came as an awful shock. **Gellert** was there in the house when it happened, and he came back to my house all of a dither, telling me he wanted to go home the next day. Terribly distressed, you know.”

> “Albus was beside himself at Ariana’s death. It was dreadful for those two brothers. They had lost everybody except each other. No wonder tempers ran high. **Aberforth blamed Albus**, as people do in such circumstances.”

> “Breaking Albus’s **nose at the funeral** was not decent. It would have destroyed **Kendra** to see her sons fighting like that across their daughter’s body. A shame **Gellert** could not have stayed for the funeral… He would have been a comfort to Albus, at least…”

---

## Questions Raised by the Funeral Brawl

This dreadful coffin-side brawl, known only to a few who attended **Ariana Dumbledore’s funeral**, raises several questions:

- Why did **Aberforth** blame **Albus** for his sister’s death?
- Was it merely a grief-driven outburst?
- Could there have been a more concrete reason for his fury?

**Grindelwald**, expelled from Durmstrang for near-fatal attacks on fellow students, fled the country hours after Ariana’s death. **Albus**, out of shame or fear, never saw Grindelwald again until forced by Wizarding world pleas.

---

## Dumbledore’s Hesitation and the Death of Ariana

Neither **Dumbledore nor Grindelwald** referred to this brief boyhood friendship later in life.

There is no doubt that Dumbledore delayed for some five years—amid turmoil, fatalities, and disappearances—before attacking Grindelwald. Possible causes:

- Lingering affection for Grindelwald.
- Fear of exposure as his once best friend.

Did Dumbledore reluctantly set out to capture the man he was once delighted to have met?

How did the mysterious **Ariana die**?

- Was she an inadvertent victim of some **Dark rite**?
- Did she stumble across something forbidden?
- Is it possible she was the first person to die **“for the greater good”**?

---

## Harry’s Reaction to the Revelations

The chapter ended and Harry looked up, shocked. Hermione finished the page and closed the book, looking alarmed.

- Harry felt a crushing disillusionment.
- He had trusted Dumbledore as the embodiment of **goodness and wisdom**.
- Now, that trust lay in **ashes**.

Hermione urged caution:

- This was written by **Rita Skeeter**.
- **“For the Greater Good”** was Grindelwald’s slogan and justification for atrocities.
- The phrase was carved over the entrance to **Nurmengard**, Grindelwald’s prison for opponents.

Harry countered:

- They were the same age as Harry and friends.
- Yet, they plotted their rise to power over Muggles while Harry risked his life fighting Dark Arts.

Hermione believed Dumbledore had changed:

- Perhaps he believed such things at 17.
- His later life was devoted to fighting Dark Arts.
- He stopped Grindelwald, voted for **Muggle protection** and **Muggle-born rights**, fought **You-Know-Who** from the start, and died trying to bring him down.

---

## The Emotional Toll on Harry

Harry expressed his anger:

- He was asked to risk his life repeatedly without full truth.
- He felt betrayed by Dumbledore’s secrecy.
- He believed Dumbledore shared more with Grindelwald than with him.

Hermione showed sympathy:

> “He loved you.”

Harry doubted:

> “I don’t know who he loved, but it wasn’t me.”

---

## Chapter 19. THE SILVER DOE

It was snowing when Hermione took over the watch at midnight.

- Harry’s dreams were disturbed, with **Nagini** weaving in and out.
- He woke panicky, imagining voices.
- Hermione suggested moving to a more sheltered place.

They Disapparated, arriving at the **Forest of Dean**.

- Hermione camped there once with her parents.
